<p><b>Giants Stadium</b> was a <a href="/wiki/Stadium" title="Stadium">stadium</a> located in <a href="/wiki/East_Rutherford,_New_Jersey" title="East Rutherford, New Jersey">East Rutherford, New Jersey</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Meadowlands_Sports_Complex" title="Meadowlands Sports Complex">Meadowlands Sports Complex</a>. The venue was open from 1976 to 2010, and primarily hosted sporting events and concerts in its history. The maximum <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> was 80,242.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The structure itself was 756 feet (230 m) long, 592 feet (180 m) wide and 144 feet (44 m) high from service level to the top of the seating bowl and 178 feet (54 m) high to the top of the south tower. The volume of the stadium was 64,500,000 cubic feet (1,830,000 m<sup>3</sup>). 13,500 tons of structural steel were used in the building process and 29,200 tons of concrete were poured.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> It was owned and operated by the <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Sports_and_Exposition_Authority" title="New Jersey Sports and Exposition Authority">New Jersey Sports and Exposition Authority</a> (NJSEA).</p>
<p>In the early 1970s the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a>, who at the time were sharing <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium_(1923)" title="Yankee Stadium (1923)">Yankee Stadium</a> with the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> baseball team, began looking for a home of their own. The Giants struck a deal with the fledgling <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Sports_and_Exposition_Authority" title="New Jersey Sports and Exposition Authority">New Jersey Sports and Exposition Authority</a> in 1971 and ground broke on the construction of the new facility in 1972. The 1972 season was the Giants' last full season in Yankee Stadium, as the ballpark was closed for a massive reconstruction following the end of the Yankees' season. Since their new stadium would take a significant amount of time to finish, and they could not use their home facility due to the construction, the Giants moved out of state and played in <a href="/wiki/New_Haven,_Connecticut" title="New Haven, Connecticut">New Haven, Connecticut</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Yale_Bowl" title="Yale Bowl">Yale Bowl</a> early in the 1973 season. After spending two years in New Haven, the Giants would return to New York for one final season in 1975 and shared <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Flushing,_Queens" title="Flushing, Queens">Flushing, Queens</a> with the Yankees, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a>. The Giants finally moved into their new home on October 10, 1976.</p>
<p>Eight years after Giants Stadium opened, it gained a second major tenant. The Jets' lease at Shea Stadium had expired at the end of the 1983 season and team owner <a href="/wiki/Leon_Hess" title="Leon Hess">Leon Hess</a> was having trouble negotiating terms of a new lease to stay in Queens. The city of New York was unwilling to agree to his terms and Hess decided to move the Jets to the Meadowlands permanently (the team previously played a regular season game there in 1977). Their first game in Giants Stadium was on September 6, 1984. With the Jets now playing at the stadium, the grounds crew needed to find a way to set their games apart from Giants games and make them more inviting for their fans and eventually came up with a series of green and white banners and coverings that were hung over the field-level blue walls that circled the stadium and (later) the four entrance gates outside the stadium.</p>
<p>The sharing of the stadium by both the Giants and Jets enabled it to break a record that had long been held by Chicago's <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field" title="Wrigley Field">Wrigley Field</a>. Entering the 2003 season, its 28th, Giants Stadium had played host to 364 NFL games, second only to the 365 played at Wrigley by the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Chicago Bears</a> in their 50 seasons there. The Giants' season opening game with the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Rams" title="Los Angeles Rams">St. Louis Rams</a> tied the record, and the following week the Jets' home opener against the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Dolphins" title="Miami Dolphins">Miami Dolphins</a> broke it.</p>
<p>Giants Stadium was closed following the <a href="/wiki/2009_NFL_season" title="2009 NFL season">2009 NFL season</a> following the construction of what is now <a href="/wiki/MetLife_Stadium" title="MetLife Stadium">MetLife Stadium</a> in the surrounding parking lot. The stadium's final event was the January 3, 2010 game featuring the Jets hosting the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bengals" title="Cincinnati Bengals">Cincinnati Bengals</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/NBC_Sunday_Night_Football" title="NBC Sunday Night Football">Sunday Night Football</a></i>. A month after the game, demolition of the structure began and was completed on August 10, 2010.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Giants Stadium was the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_leagues_of_the_United_States_and_Canada" title="Major professional sports leagues of the United States and Canada">major league</a> sporting venue in <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> (though the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Dodgers" title="Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a> had played seven home games at <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Stadium" title="Roosevelt Stadium">Roosevelt Stadium</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jersey_City" title="Jersey City">Jersey City</a> in 1956 &amp; 1957), and its success, along with that of the Giants in the 1980s was a major impetus behind increased pride and enthusiasm among New Jersey residents.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_year_in_business">First year in business</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: First year in business">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Giants Stadium opened on October 10, 1976, as 76,042 fans witnessed a loss by the Giants to the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a>. The Giants had played their first four games on the road that season. <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">College football</a> made its debut at Giants Stadium on October 23, 1976, with <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Scarlet_Knights_football" title="Rutgers Scarlet Knights football">Rutgers University</a> defeating <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Lions" title="Columbia Lions">Columbia</a> 47–0 and extending their winning streak to 14 games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The New York Giants played their season-opening home game in the stadium on September 18 of the <a href="/wiki/1977_NFL_season" title="1977 NFL season">1977 season</a> (a 20–17 win over the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Redskins" title="Washington Redskins">Washington Redskins</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_pro_football_teams_that_have_used_Giants_Stadium">Other pro football teams that have used Giants Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Other pro football teams that have used Giants Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Other professional football teams that have called Giants Stadium home over the years include the <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Generals" title="New Jersey Generals">New Jersey Generals</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Football_League" title="United States Football League">USFL</a>; the <a href="/wiki/New_York/New_Jersey_Knights" title="New York/New Jersey Knights">New York/New Jersey Knights</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_League_of_American_Football" title="World League of American Football">World League of American Football</a>; the <a href="/wiki/New_York/New_Jersey_Hitmen" title="New York/New Jersey Hitmen">New York/New Jersey Hitmen</a> of the <a href="/wiki/XFL" title="XFL">XFL</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Sentinels" title="New York Sentinels">New York Sentinels</a> (who played one game at the stadium in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Football_League_(2009)" title="United Football League (2009)">United Football League</a>'s inaugural season). The 1985 USFL championship game which turned out to be the last USFL game played was held at Giants Stadium.</p>
<p>In the second week of the <a href="/wiki/2005_NFL_season" title="2005 NFL season">2005 season</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2005_New_Orleans_Saints_season" title="2005 New Orleans Saints season">New Orleans Saints</a> used the stadium for a "home" game against the Giants because of extensive damage to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louisiana_Superdome" title="Louisiana Superdome">Louisiana Superdome</a> after <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a>. One <a href="/wiki/End_zone" title="End zone">end zone</a> was painted in Saints colors, Saints banners were hung on the walls around the sidelines, and the Saints wore their home jerseys. The game was rescheduled to a Monday night with a special start time of 7:30 PM <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">EDT</a>, preceding the other scheduled game on <i><a href="/wiki/Monday_Night_Football" title="Monday Night Football">Monday Night Football</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The Giants were normally not visitors at Giants Stadium unless they were playing the Jets.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="College_football_games">College football games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: College football games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The stadium hosted college football games, including the <a href="/wiki/Garden_State_Bowl" title="Garden State Bowl">Garden State Bowl</a> from 1978–1981; the <a href="/wiki/Kickoff_Classic" title="Kickoff Classic">Kickoff Classic</a> from 1983 to 2002; the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=New_York_Urban_League_Classic&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="New York Urban League Classic (page does not exist)">New York Urban League Classic</a> since 1981; a number of Rutgers homes games (including all their home games during the <a href="/wiki/1993_NCAA_Division_I-A_football_season" title="1993 NCAA Division I-A football season">1993 season</a>); several <a href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_Fighting_Irish_football" title="Notre Dame Fighting Irish football">Notre Dame</a>–<a href="/wiki/Navy_Midshipmen_football" title="Navy Midshipmen football">Navy</a> and Notre Dame–<a href="/wiki/Army_Black_Knights_football" title="Army Black Knights football">Army</a> games; and the <a href="/wiki/Army%E2%80%93Navy_Game" title="Army–Navy Game">Army–Navy Game</a> on three occasions, most recently in <a href="/wiki/2002_NCAA_Division_I-A_football_season" title="2002 NCAA Division I-A football season">2002</a>. <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_Orange_football" title="Syracuse Orange football">Syracuse</a> also played two home games at Giants Stadium during the <a href="/wiki/1979_NCAA_Division_I-A_football_season" title="1979 NCAA Division I-A football season">1979 season</a>, against <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Mountaineers_football" title="West Virginia Mountaineers football">West Virginia</a> and <a href="/wiki/1979_Penn_State_Nittany_Lions_football_team" title="1979 Penn State Nittany Lions football team">Penn State</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Carrier_Dome" title="Carrier Dome">Carrier Dome</a> was under construction. Columbia also played some home games at Giants Stadium in <a href="/wiki/1983_NCAA_Division_I-A_football_season" title="1983 NCAA Division I-A football season">1983</a>, due to construction at its home stadium. <a href="/wiki/Temple_Owls_football" title="Temple Owls football">Temple</a>, needing a home field due to a schedule conflict with <a href="/wiki/Veterans_Stadium" title="Veterans Stadium">Veterans Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, used Giants Stadium as their home field versus <a href="/wiki/Penn_State_Nittany_Lions_football" title="Penn State Nittany Lions football">Penn State</a> in September <a href="/wiki/1996_NCAA_Division_I-A_football_season" title="1996 NCAA Division I-A football season">1996</a>. <a href="/wiki/Princeton_Tigers" title="Princeton Tigers">Princeton</a> also played one home game at Giants Stadium (against <a href="/wiki/Yale_Bulldogs_football" title="Yale Bulldogs football">Yale</a>) during the construction of Princeton's new stadium in <a href="/wiki/1997_NCAA_Division_I-A_football_season" title="1997 NCAA Division I-A football season">1997</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Soccer_at_Giants_Stadium">Soccer at Giants Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Soccer at Giants Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NY_Red_Bulls_vs_LA_Galaxy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/NY_Red_Bulls_vs_LA_Galaxy.jpg/300px-NY_Red_Bulls_vs_LA_Galaxy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/NY_Red_Bulls_vs_LA_Galaxy.jpg/450px-NY_Red_Bulls_vs_LA_Galaxy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/NY_Red_Bulls_vs_LA_Galaxy.jpg/600px-NY_Red_Bulls_vs_LA_Galaxy.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NY_Red_Bulls_vs_LA_Galaxy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A New York Red Bulls match at Giants Stadium in 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Cosmos_(1971%E2%80%931985)" title="New York Cosmos (1971–1985)">New York Cosmos</a> of the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Soccer_League_(1968%E2%80%9384)" title="North American Soccer League (1968–84)">North American Soccer League</a> moved to Giants Stadium for the 1977 season and remained until the league folded in 1985. The NASL championship game <a href="/wiki/Soccer_Bowl_%2778" title="Soccer Bowl '78">Soccer Bowl '78</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soccer_Bowl_%2779" title="Soccer Bowl '79">Soccer Bowl '79</a> were held at Giants Stadium.</p>
<p>Seven games of the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 FIFA World Cup</a> soccer tournament were held at Giants Stadium (including the <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> v <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_national_football_team" title="Bulgaria national football team">Bulgaria</a> semi-final), along with several games of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup_1999" title="FIFA Women's World Cup 1999">1999 Women's World Cup</a>.</p>
<p>In 2003, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SuperCoppa_Italiana" title="SuperCoppa Italiana">SuperCoppa Italiana</a>, an annual match pitting the winners of <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> (Italy's top division) and the <a href="/wiki/Coppa_Italia" title="Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> (Italian Cup), was held in Giants Stadium instead of in Italy because both clubs involved (<a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus F.C.</a> and <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">A.C. Milan</a>) were touring the United States late in the summer, when the event is normally scheduled.</p>
<p>In 2005, the stadium played host to several matches in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CONCACAF_Gold_Cup_2005" title="CONCACAF Gold Cup 2005">CONCACAF Gold Cup</a>, including the final, which saw the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">USA</a> defeat <a href="/wiki/Panama_national_football_team" title="Panama national football team">Panama</a>, 3–1 in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penalty_shootout_(football)" title="Penalty shootout (football)">penalty shootout</a> after the sides played to a scoreless draw. It again held the final 4 years later for the <a href="/wiki/2009_CONCACAF_Gold_Cup" title="2009 CONCACAF Gold Cup">CONCACAF Gold Cup</a> which saw <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> defeat the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">USA</a> 5–0.</p>
<p>It has seen many European soccer tours in recent years, hosting games involving such major soccer clubs as <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers</a>.</p>
<p>It also hosted <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a>'s 3–2 victory over <a href="/wiki/Colombia_national_football_team" title="Colombia national football team">Colombia</a> on May 31, 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Red_Bulls" title="New York Red Bulls">New York Red Bulls</a> (formerly the New York/New Jersey MetroStars) of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a> played at the stadium for their first 14 seasons. They moved to the soccer-specific <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Arena_(MLS)" title="Red Bull Arena (MLS)">Red Bull Arena</a> in nearby <a href="/wiki/Harrison,_New_Jersey" title="Harrison, New Jersey">Harrison, New Jersey</a> in 2010.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1989_Marlboro_Cup_.28New_York.29">1989 Marlboro Cup (New York)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1989 Marlboro Cup (New York)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1996_.26_1997_Major_League_Soccer_All-Star_Games">1996 &amp; 1997 Major League Soccer All-Star Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 1996 &amp; 1997 Major League Soccer All-Star Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Giants Stadium hosted the first two <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Soccer All-Star Game">Major League Soccer All-Star Game</a>'s ever played. The games were played in East vs. West format. The 1996 game was the first game of a doubleheader. That second game was between <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazilian soccer team</a> and a team of FIFA All-Stars</p>
<p><b>1996:</b></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pope_John_Paul_II_at_Giants_Stadium">Pope John Paul II at Giants Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Pope John Paul II at Giants Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The second largest crowd to ever attend an event at Giants Stadium was 82,948, as <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> celebrated Mass during a rainstorm on October 5, 1995. The record was broken on September 24, 2009 with an attendance of 84,472 at the <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> concert.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Concerts">Concerts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Concerts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Giants_Stadium_2006.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Giants_Stadium_2006.jpg/300px-Giants_Stadium_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Giants_Stadium_2006.jpg/450px-Giants_Stadium_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Giants_Stadium_2006.jpg/600px-Giants_Stadium_2006.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Giants_Stadium_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Giants Stadium in 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The stadium played host to <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>'s final <a href="/wiki/A_Conspiracy_of_Hope" title="A Conspiracy of Hope">A Conspiracy of Hope</a> Benefit Concert on June 15, 1986. The show was a sold-out, all-day event, running from noon until 11 p.m. and broadcast on <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>. The show was headlined by <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a> and also featured <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Adams" title="Bryan Adams">Bryan Adams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Gabriel" title="Peter Gabriel">Peter Gabriel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Baez" title="Joan Baez">Joan Baez</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Neville_Brothers" title="The Neville Brothers">The Neville Brothers</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Police" title="The Police">The Police</a>. Additional artists that performed include <a href="/wiki/John_Eddie" title="John Eddie">John Eddie</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Max_Weinberg" title="Max Weinberg">Max Weinberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Third_World_(band)" title="Third World (band)">Third World</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hooters" title="The Hooters">The Hooters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter,_Paul_and_Mary" title="Peter, Paul and Mary">Peter, Paul and Mary</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steven_van_Zandt" title="Steven van Zandt">Steven van Zandt</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Bob_Geldof" title="Bob Geldof">Bob Geldof</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Jordan" title="Stanley Jordan">Stanley Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Armatrading" title="Joan Armatrading">Joan Armatrading</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Browne" title="Jackson Browne">Jackson Browne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A9n_Blades" title="Rubén Blades">Rubén Blades</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Fela_Kuti" title="Fela Kuti">Fela Kuti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Santana" title="Carlos Santana">Carlos Santana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yoko_Ono" title="Yoko Ono">Yoko Ono</a>, <a href="/wiki/Howard_Jones_(musician)" title="Howard Jones (musician)">Howard Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miles_Davis" title="Miles Davis">Miles Davis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joni_Mitchell" title="Joni Mitchell">Joni Mitchell</a>. Spoken introductions were made by <a href="/wiki/Billy_Graham" title="Billy Graham">Billy Graham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Bradley" title="Bill Bradley">Bill Bradley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daryl_Hannah" title="Daryl Hannah">Daryl Hannah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_De_Niro" title="Robert De Niro">Robert De Niro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Reeve" title="Christopher Reeve">Christopher Reeve</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_J._Fox" title="Michael J. Fox">Michael J. Fox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali" title="Muhammad Ali">Muhammad Ali</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend" title="Pete Townshend">Pete Townshend</a> was scheduled to perform, but cancelled at the last minute, when his father, Cliff Townshend, became gravely ill, which would have been his first US solo appearance. This also marked The Police's final full-live performance together, until their <a href="/wiki/The_Police_Reunion_Tour" title="The Police Reunion Tour">2007 Reunion Tour</a>, 21 years later.</p>
<p>The stadium played host to The <a href="/wiki/Tattoo_the_Earth" title="Tattoo the Earth">Tattoo the Earth</a> Tour on July 20, 2000. The show featured performances by <a href="/wiki/Slipknot_(band)" title="Slipknot (band)">Slipknot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slayer" title="Slayer">Slayer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sevendust" title="Sevendust">Sevendust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sepultura" title="Sepultura">Sepultura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hed_PE" title="Hed PE">Hed PE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mudvayne" title="Mudvayne">Mudvayne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Downset." title="Downset.">downset.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hatebreed" title="Hatebreed">Hatebreed</a>, <a href="/wiki/Full_Devil_Jacket" title="Full Devil Jacket">Full Devil Jacket</a>, Famous, <a href="/wiki/Amen_(American_band)" title="Amen (American band)">Amen</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.P.O." title="U.P.O.">U.P.O.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nothingface" title="Nothingface">Nothingface</a>, PPM, <a href="/wiki/Cold_(band)" title="Cold (band)">Cold</a>, Relative Ash, <a href="/wiki/Systematic_(band)" title="Systematic (band)">Systematic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Six_Feet_Under_(band)" title="Six Feet Under (band)">Six Feet Under</a>, <a href="/wiki/Candiria" title="Candiria">Candiria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lamb_of_God_(band)" title="Lamb of God (band)">Lamb of God</a>, <a href="/wiki/God_Forbid" title="God Forbid">God Forbid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darkest_Hour_(band)" title="Darkest Hour (band)">Darkest Hour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unearth" title="Unearth">Unearth</a>, <a href="/wiki/All_That_Remains_(band)" title="All That Remains (band)">All That Remains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dropkick_Murphys" title="Dropkick Murphys">Dropkick Murphys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sick_of_It_All" title="Sick of It All">Sick of It All</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Army" title="Tiger Army">Tiger Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Converge_(band)" title="Converge (band)">Converge</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Unseen_(band)" title="The Unseen (band)">The Unseen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reach_the_Sky" title="Reach the Sky">Reach the Sky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stretch_Arm_Strong" title="Stretch Arm Strong">Stretch Arm Strong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kill_Your_Idols" title="Kill Your Idols">Kill Your Idols</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nashville_Pussy" title="Nashville Pussy">Nashville Pussy</a>, including the only appearance by <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a> during the tour and also featured 42 tattoo artists from Australia, Austria, France, Germany, Malaysia, Manitoba, Spain, Switzerland and the US.</p>
<p>The stadium has also played host to music festivals, including The <a href="/wiki/Monsters_of_Rock_Tour_1988" title="Monsters of Rock Tour 1988">Monsters of Rock Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_at_the_Meadowlands" title="Music at the Meadowlands">Music at the Meadowlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ozzfest" title="Ozzfest">Ozzfest</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Bamboozle" title="The Bamboozle">The Bamboozle</a> (in the parking lot, annually, since 2003).</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dave_Matthews_Band" title="Dave Matthews Band">Dave Matthews Band</a> played the stadium 9 times from 1998–2001, including three nights each in 2000 and 2001. On June 11, 2001 (the first of three nights), the band played the song "Two Step", where Dave Matthews sung the improvisational lyrics "let it rain", where then a thunderstorm broke out. This has been called "Two Step In The Rain" by fans, and can be heard on <a href="/wiki/The_Best_of_What%27s_Around_Vol._1" title="The Best of What's Around Vol. 1">The Best of What's Around Vol. 1</a>. When Matthews learned of the closing of Giants Stadium, he said "I can't imagine I'll ever fall in love with a stadium like I did with Giants Stadium."</p>
<p>Many locals say it is the home turf of <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a> &amp; The <a href="/wiki/E_Street_Band" title="E Street Band">E Street Band</a>, due to the fact that they came from <a href="/wiki/Freehold_Township,_New_Jersey" title="Freehold Township, New Jersey">Freehold, New Jersey</a>. Several songs on his 1986 live album <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live/1975-85" title="Live/1975-85">Live/1975-85</a></i> were recorded at shows at the stadium in August 1985.</p>
<p>Springsteen wrote the song "Wrecking Ball" in response to the closing of the stadium and in 2009 performed it for the first time at the final five concerts at Giants Stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> It would go on to be the title track of his next studio album, released over two years later.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seating_Capacity">Seating Capacity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Seating Capacity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> over the years went as the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>76,891 (1976–1993)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></li>
<li>77,121 (1994)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></li>
<li>78,148 (1995–1998)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></li>
<li>79,469 (1999–2001)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></li>
<li>80,242 (2002–2010)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demolition">Demolition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Demolition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Demolition work on Giants Stadium began at approximately 10:00 AM EST on February 4, 2010 at the Gate B spirals, the closest point to the new stadium. The demolition work was expected to cost more than $10 million and took approximately four months to complete.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> As of May 10, 2010 approximately 50% of the Stadium had been demolished. On May 19, 2010 at 8:30pm, demolition crews pulled down the press box, the highest part of the stadium. In the early afternoon of June 28, 2010, the last section of stadium grandstand came down, leaving just two later demolished upper level escalators standing.</p>
<p>Much of the stadium's memorabilia was sold to a sports memorabilia company, such as the framed pictures from the suites, all of the building's signage and a good portion of the saved bowl seats. Other property was liquidated to other NJSEA facilities such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IZOD_Center" title="IZOD Center">IZOD Center</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monmouth_Park" title="Monmouth Park">Monmouth Park</a> Racetrack.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Changes_and_co-tenants">Changes and co-tenants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Changes and co-tenants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Giants_Stadium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1335" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Giants_Stadium.jpg/300px-Giants_Stadium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Giants_Stadium.jpg/450px-Giants_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Giants_Stadium.jpg/600px-Giants_Stadium.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Giants_Stadium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Giants Stadium during a December 17, 2005 game between the Giants and <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Chiefs" title="Kansas City Chiefs">Kansas City Chiefs</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To accommodate these varied events, Giants Stadium sported various playing surfaces in its history. From its opening until the end of the 1999 NFL season, Giants Stadium sported an <a href="/wiki/AstroTurf" title="AstroTurf">AstroTurf</a> playing surface. This surface was covered by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bermuda_grass" title="Bermuda grass">Bermuda grass</a> <a href="/wiki/Sod" title="Sod">sod</a> for the World Cup in 1994, identical to that at the <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_(stadium)" title="Rose Bowl (stadium)">Rose Bowl</a> where the other semifinal and the finals were held (so that both teams in the finals would have played on identical surfaces). The grass was removed after the World Cup, as it would have died in the New Jersey winter. The MetroStars installed a grass field with interchangeable trays each spring that was removed prior to football season, forcing the team to play the remainder of its season on the AstroTurf field used by the football teams. (It should be noted that when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Cosmos_(1971%E2%80%931985)" title="New York Cosmos (1971–1985)">New York Cosmos</a> called Giants Stadium home, they played on the stadium's artificial surface and never used a grass field.)</p>
<p>The AstroTurf was replaced in 2000 by a system of interchangeable grass trays similar to those put in place for soccer, but was kept in place under the trays to aid in draining the field when it got wet. Over the next three years, the conditions would worsen as the season went on and the field quality was typically rated just as low as the old, hard AstroTurf had been. Giants Stadium finally scrapped the grass in favor of <a href="/wiki/FieldTurf" title="FieldTurf">FieldTurf</a> for the 2003 season, a surface which remained in place until the stadium closed.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a> left <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a> and moved to Giants Stadium in 1984 after years of suffering under onerous lease terms imposed at the insistence of baseball's <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>. When they moved across the Hudson, many predicted the stadium would be renamed. While the Jets were attracted by the stadium's larger capacity (it held 15,000 more seats than Shea did in its football configuration), they were understandably displeased at the prospect of playing in a facility named after another team. However, under the terms of the stadium lease, changing the name of the stadium required the approval of the Giants, and they were unwilling to do so. As such, for years afterward the Jets referred to Giants Stadium as "The Meadowlands" whenever they played there.</p>
<p>Thanks largely to the dual occupancy of Giants Stadium by two NFL teams since 1984, it surpassed <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field" title="Wrigley Field">Wrigley Field</a> (home of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Chicago Bears</a> for 50 seasons) as the venue to have hosted more NFL games than any other in league history. The game played between the <a href="/wiki/2003_New_York_Jets_season" title="2003 New York Jets season">Jets</a> and <a href="/wiki/2003_Miami_Dolphins_season" title="2003 Miami Dolphins season">Miami Dolphins</a> on September 14, 2003 was the 366th regular season NFL game at Giants Stadium breaking Wrigley's regular season record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the stadium was originally built for the Giants, the stadium's lower walls were blue and the seats and the stadium's four gates were red and blue to reflect the team colors. When the Jets moved in, green banners were hung over the walls and eventually over the outer gates of the stadium anytime the team hosted a game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> In addition, team-specific endzone decorations would be changed for Jets home games. This was accomplished by either painting over the Giants logos, or replacing the turf section of each endzone. Midfield decorations at the 50-yard line were typically not team-specific (in early years a Meadowlands logo, and later a NFL shield), which could be used for both teams' games.</p>
<p>In mid-December, traditionally the stadium hosted a Saturday-Sunday NFL doubleheader, with the Giants playing a home game one day and the Jets playing the other. The night between the games was a challenge for the stadium grounds crew, as they only had hours to convert the stadium from one team's colors to the other. As per the NFL schedule, the Giants and the Jets play each other once every four years. In that case, there was a predetermined home team, and a predetermined away team. In those games, the away team gets a rare away game in their own home stadium. The Giants and Jets typically play each other every year in the third week of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Football_League_exhibition_season" title="National Football League exhibition season">NFL Preseason</a>, and the teams annually rotated the home and away teams.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Jimmy_Hoffa_urban_legend">The Jimmy Hoffa urban legend</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: The Jimmy Hoffa urban legend">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>For some years, a popular urban legend purported that the remains of <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Hoffa" title="Jimmy Hoffa">Jimmy Hoffa</a>, whose disappearance coincided with construction of the stadium, had been buried under one of the end zones at the field.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> This led <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> to suggest that this "takes on special meaning when a punter goes for the '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coffin_corner_(football)" title="Coffin corner (football)">coffin corner</a>.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In a similar vein, sportscaster <a href="/wiki/Marv_Albert" title="Marv Albert">Marv Albert</a> once said that a team was "kicking towards the Hoffa end of the field." This was tested by the <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Channel" title="Discovery Channel">Discovery Channel</a> show <i><a href="/wiki/MythBusters" title="MythBusters">MythBusters</a></i>, and they were unable to find any sign of a body.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_moments">Notable moments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notable moments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>October 10, 1976: The Giants played their first ever regular season game at Giants Stadium, a 24–14 loss to the Dallas Cowboys in front of 76,042 in attendance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></li>
<li>October 1, 1977: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_(soccer)" title="Football (soccer)">Soccer</a> legend <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pelé">Pelé</a> played his last game, an exhibition match between the Cosmos and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santos_Futebol_Clube" title="Santos Futebol Clube">Santos</a>. He played the first half for the Cosmos and the second half for his old Brazilian team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
<li>October 28, 1978: <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_Scarlet_Knights_football" title="Rutgers Scarlet Knights football">Rutgers</a> beat <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Lions" title="Columbia Lions">Columbia</a> 69–0. The Lions' humiliating defeat was the last game in one of the oldest rivalries in <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a>. Columbia's young coach <a href="/wiki/William_Campbell_(business_executive)" title="William Campbell (business executive)">Bill Campbell</a> retired from coaching after the game and went on to a vastly more successful career in the <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></li>
<li>November 19, 1978: Giants quarterback <a href="/wiki/Joe_Pisarcik" title="Joe Pisarcik">Joe Pisarcik</a> fumbled the handoff to <a href="/wiki/Larry_Csonka" title="Larry Csonka">Larry Csonka</a> with just seconds remaining in the game, allowing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herman_Edwards" title="Herman Edwards">Herman Edwards</a> (later a Jets head coach) to scoop it up and run it back for a touchdown, giving the Philadelphia Eagles an improbable 19–17 win. This play would be known as "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Miracle_at_the_Meadowlands" title="The Miracle at the Meadowlands">The Miracle at the Meadowlands</a>", and helped lead to the hiring of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ray_Perkins_(wide_receiver)" title="Ray Perkins (wide receiver)">Ray Perkins</a> as head coach, and later <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Young_(football_executive)" title="George Young (football executive)">George Young</a> as general manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Pisarcik's career in New York never recovered, and <a href="/wiki/Phil_Simms" title="Phil Simms">Phil Simms</a> was drafted shortly after.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></li>
<li>September 6, 1984: The New York Jets moved into Giants Stadium, losing their first game to the Pittsburgh Steelers by a score of 23–17.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li>July 29, 30 and 31, 1984: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Jacksons" title="The Jacksons">The Jacksons</a> performed three sold out shows during their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victory_Tour_(The_Jacksons_5_tour)" title="Victory Tour (The Jacksons 5 tour)">Victory Tour</a> in front of 136.000 in attendance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li>July 14, 1985: The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore_Stars" title="Baltimore Stars">Baltimore Stars</a> defeat the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Invaders" title="Oakland Invaders">Oakland Invaders</a>, 28–24, in the 1985 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USFL" title="USFL">USFL</a> Championship Game, the final game in league history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>August–September 1985: <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a> and The <a href="/wiki/E_Street_Band" title="E Street Band">E Street Band</a> performed six sold out shows on the final leg of their <a href="/wiki/Born_in_the_U.S.A._Tour" title="Born in the U.S.A. Tour">Born in the U.S.A. Tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 28–29, 1985: Giants Stadium makes history by playing host to multiple playoff games in the same weekend. The Jets host the first playoff game in stadium history, as well as their first since hosting the <a href="/wiki/1981_Buffalo_Bills_season" title="1981 Buffalo Bills season">Buffalo Bills</a> in 1981 at <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a>,on December 28, losing to the eventual AFC champion <a href="/wiki/1985_New_England_Patriots_season" title="1985 New England Patriots season">New England Patriots</a> 26-14 in the AFC Wild Card Game. The next day the Giants, who are playing their first playoff game at home since they lost the <a href="/wiki/1962_NFL_Championship_Game" title="1962 NFL Championship Game">1962 NFL Championship Game</a> at <a href="/wiki/Yankee_Stadium_(1923)" title="Yankee Stadium (1923)">Yankee Stadium</a>, defeat the defending Super Bowl champion <a href="/wiki/1985_San_Francisco_49ers_season" title="1985 San Francisco 49ers season">San Francisco 49ers</a> 17-3 in the NFC Wild Card Game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></li>
<li>January 11, 1987: The <a href="/wiki/1986_New_York_Giants_season" title="1986 New York Giants season">New York Giants</a> shut out the <a href="/wiki/1986_Washington_Redskins_season" title="1986 Washington Redskins season">Washington Redskins</a> 17–0 in the NFC Championship game to advance to <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXI" title="Super Bowl XXI">Super Bowl XXI</a> in Pasadena. Two weeks later, the Giants would win <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXI" title="Super Bowl XXI">Super Bowl XXI</a>, their first Super Bowl victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></li>
<li>November 8, 1987: The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a> defeated the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a> 17–10 in ESPN's first televised regular season game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 18, 1988: In a testament to the <a href="/wiki/Giants%E2%80%93Jets_rivalry" title="Giants–Jets rivalry">Giants–Jets rivalry</a>, the Jets helped eliminate the Giants from playoff contention in the final week of the <a href="/wiki/1988_NFL_season" title="1988 NFL season">1988 regular season</a>. Jets quarterback <a href="/wiki/Ken_O%27Brien" title="Ken O'Brien">Ken O'Brien</a> threw a touchdown pass to wide receiver <a href="/wiki/Al_Toon" title="Al Toon">Al Toon</a> with 39 seconds left to give the Jets a 27–21 victory. The Giants were mathematically eliminated when their loss was combined with the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Eagles" title="Philadelphia Eagles">Philadelphia Eagles</a> victory over the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Rams" title="Los Angeles Rams">Los Angeles Rams</a>' 38–16 victory over the eventual Super Bowl champion <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers" title="San Francisco 49ers">San Francisco 49ers</a> due to tiebreakers.</li>
<li>June 30, 1989: <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">The Who</a> sold out four consecutive shows performing portions of the rock opera <i><a href="/wiki/Tommy_(1975_film)" title="Tommy (1975 film)">Tommy</a></i> to open the first of two sets each night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></li>
<li>June–July 1994: Giants Stadium served as a venue for the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 FIFA World Cup</a>, opening with <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Ireland</a>'s 1–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a>, and concluding with Italy's 2–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_national_football_team" title="Bulgaria national football team">Bulgaria</a> in the semifinals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></li>
<li>July 18, 1994: <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a> performed their final US show ever on their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_Bell_Tour" title="Division Bell Tour">Division Bell Tour</a> in which they performed <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Side_of_the_Moon" title="The Dark Side of the Moon">The Dark Side of the Moon</a></i> in its entirety..</li>
<li>October 19, 1997: Following the <a href="/wiki/1997_New_York_Jets_season" title="1997 New York Jets season">Jets</a> defeating the <a href="/wiki/1997_New_England_Patriots_season" title="1997 New England Patriots season">Patriots</a>, two individuals were violently accosted and stabbed by an underage and drunken Patriots fan. The incident would lead to various lawsuits and the establishment of higher security standards and no alcohol being served after the 3rd quarter at Giants Stadium.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>December 13, 1998: The <a href="/wiki/1998_New_York_Giants_season" title="1998 New York Giants season">New York Giants</a> defeated the then-13–0 <a href="/wiki/1998_Denver_Broncos_season" title="1998 Denver Broncos season">Denver Broncos</a> 20–16 in front of 72,336 in attendance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></li>
<li>October 23, 2000: In what has been called the greatest game on <i><a href="/wiki/Monday_Night_Football" title="Monday Night Football">Monday Night Football</a></i>, the New York Jets came back from a 30–7 deficit by scoring 30 points in the fourth quarter and another 3 in overtime to beat the Miami Dolphins 40–37. The game is known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Monday_Night_Miracle_(American_football)" title="The Monday Night Miracle (American football)">the Monday Night Miracle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Giants_Stadion.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Giants_Stadion.jpg/300px-Giants_Stadion.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Giants_Stadion.jpg/450px-Giants_Stadion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8e/Giants_Stadion.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Giants_Stadion.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
New York Jets playing at Giants Stadium, November 2001</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>January 14, 2001: On a field of painted mud, the New York Giants defeated the Minnesota Vikings 41–0 in the NFC Championship Game in front of 79,310 in attendance to send the Giants to <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXV" title="Super Bowl XXXV">Super Bowl XXXV</a> in Tampa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li>July–August 2003: <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a> and the <a href="/wiki/E_Street_Band" title="E Street Band">E Street Band</a> broke their own record with 10 sold-out shows on <a href="/wiki/The_Rising_Tour" title="The Rising Tour">the Rising Tour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 20, 2003: The <a href="/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a> defeated the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a> 21-16 in ESPN's 200th NFL regular season game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li>
<li>October 10, 2004: The Television show <i><a href="/wiki/Queer_Eye" title="Queer Eye">Queer Eye</a> For The Straight Guy</i> filmed "A Pigskin Proposal" prior to and during a New York Jets home game. It featured a pregame tailgating party and a halftime proposal where Brian Mortensen proposed to Rachel Groeneveld.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></li>
<li>September 1, 2005: The punk rock band <a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">Green Day</a> sold out Giants Stadium with <a href="/wiki/Against_Me!" title="Against Me!">Against Me!</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Eat_World" title="Jimmy Eat World">Jimmy Eat World</a>. It was their biggest concert played in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 26, 2005: The New York Jets &amp; The New England Patriots played each other in a classic battle on the last Monday Night Football game on ABC. The Patriots defeated the Jets 31–21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></li>
<li>January 8, 2006: The largest crowd to witness a Giant game, 79,378, watched a Giants 23–0 playoff loss to the Carolina Panthers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></li>
<li>July 29, 2006: <a href="/wiki/Bon_Jovi" title="Bon Jovi">Bon Jovi</a> played their eighth consecutive sell-out of Giants Stadium. This was also the last concert of their <a href="/wiki/Have_a_Nice_Day_Tour" title="Have a Nice Day Tour">Have a Nice Day Tour</a>.</li>
<li>July 7, 2007: The "New York" portion of <a href="/wiki/Live_Earth" title="Live Earth">Live Earth</a>, a worldwide series of concerts of pop and rock music featuring various bands and musical artists planned to inspire global warming activism, was held at Giants Stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kenna" title="Kenna">Kenna</a>, <a href="/wiki/KT_Tunstall" title="KT Tunstall">KT Tunstall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taking_Back_Sunday" title="Taking Back Sunday">Taking Back Sunday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Urban" title="Keith Urban">Keith Urban</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a>, <a href="/wiki/AFI_(band)" title="AFI (band)">AFI</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fall_Out_Boy" title="Fall Out Boy">Fall Out Boy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akon" title="Akon">Akon</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Mayer" title="John Mayer">John Mayer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melissa_Etheridge" title="Melissa Etheridge">Melissa Etheridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Matthews_Band" title="Dave Matthews Band">Dave Matthews Band</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Clarkson" title="Kelly Clarkson">Kelly Clarkson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Smashing_Pumpkins" title="The Smashing Pumpkins">The Smashing Pumpkins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Waters" title="Roger Waters">Roger Waters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bon_Jovi" title="Bon Jovi">Bon Jovi</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Police" title="The Police">The Police</a> all performed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>August 5, 2007: <a href="/wiki/The_Police" title="The Police">The Police</a> performed in front of 55, 000 people on there <a href="/wiki/The_Police_Reunion_Tour" title="The Police Reunion Tour">The Police Reunion Tour</a>. The band first performed here in 1986 at the <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_Conspiracy_of_Hope_Tour" title="A Conspiracy of Hope Tour">A Conspiracy of Hope Tour</a>, and again for Live Earth. <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting (musician)</a> had been here 3 addition times on his own as well. 2 times in 1993 when he opened for the <a href="/wiki/Grateful_Dead" title="Grateful Dead">Grateful Dead</a>, and once in 1999 for <a href="/wiki/NetAid" title="NetAid">NetAid</a>. This however was the band's 3rd and last appearance at the stadium for a concert, and there first concert to take place on a tour stop instead of a charity concert.</li>
<li>August 18, 2007: 66,237 attended as the largest crowd ever for a regular-season <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">MLS</a> match at Giants Stadium (or any match between two MLS teams here).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Red_Bulls" title="New York Red Bulls">MetroStars/Red Bulls</a> previously had several matches with 50,000–65,000, and this day's match was also their highest attendance home or away for a regular-season match. This <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Galaxy" title="Los Angeles Galaxy">LA Galaxy</a> versus Red Bulls match also set a new high for an MLS match that was not a part of a double-header, even beating the highest MLS Cup Final attendance (in 2002: 61,316).</li>
<li>September 9, 2007: <a href="/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a> CB Ellis Hobbs set an NFL record by taking the second-half kickoff 108 yards for a touchdown against the New York Jets in a 38–14 opening day victory. The play also tied the record for the longest play in NFL history at the time, matching the 108-yard missed field goal returns by the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Chicago Bears</a>' <a href="/wiki/Devin_Hester" title="Devin Hester">Devin Hester</a> against the Giants in 2006, and the Bears' <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Vasher" title="Nathan Vasher">Nathan Vasher</a> the previous season against San Francisco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> That record was broken 8 weeks later when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego_Chargers" title="San Diego Chargers">San Diego Chargers</a> CB Antonio Cromartie returned a missed field-goal 109 yards for a touchdown against the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Vikings" title="Minnesota Vikings">Minnesota Vikings</a>.</li>
<li>December 29, 2007: The New England Patriots closed out their undefeated 16–0 regular season at Giants Stadium with a 38–35 <a href="/wiki/2007_New_England_Patriots%E2%80%93New_York_Giants_game" title="2007 New England Patriots–New York Giants game">win</a> over the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a> in front of a record regular season crowd on 79,110. In the fourth quarter, Patriots QB <a href="/wiki/Tom_Brady" title="Tom Brady">Tom Brady</a> broke <a href="/wiki/Peyton_Manning" title="Peyton Manning">Peyton Manning</a>'s NFL record of 49 TD passes set in 2004, with his NFL record 50th TD pass, a 65-yard touchdown pass to wide receiver <a href="/wiki/Randy_Moss" title="Randy Moss">Randy Moss</a>, who on the same play set the record for most touchdown receptions in a single season with 23, breaking the record held previously by <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Rice" title="Jerry Rice">Jerry Rice</a> with 22 touchdown receptions set in 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li>June 8, 2008: The <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">USA</a> played then world #1 Argentina to a scoreless draw in front of a crowd of 78,682.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></li>
<li>July 26, 2009: In the <a href="/wiki/2009_CONCACAF_Gold_Cup" title="2009 CONCACAF Gold Cup">2009 CONCACAF Gold Cup</a> Final 79,156 fans witnessed <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> beat the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men's national soccer team">USA</a> 5–0, Mexico's first win against the USA on American soil in a decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></li>
<li>September 23–24, 2009: <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> played two consecutive sold out shows at Giants Stadium, their last two shows of the famous venue, as part of their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U2_360" title="U2 360">U2 360</a> tour. On the second night of the performance, Bono announced that the attendance record has been broken. He also joked that "not even the pope had as many people there." The final attendance was 84,467.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></li>
<li>October 9, 2009: <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a> and the <a href="/wiki/E_Street_Band" title="E Street Band">E Street Band</a> played in the final concert at Giants Stadium. The concert capped a five-night stand of performances in September and October, highlighting Springsteen's classic albums, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Born_To_Run" title="Born To Run">Born To Run</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Darkness_on_the_Edge_of_Town" title="Darkness on the Edge of Town">Darkness on the Edge of Town</a></i>, and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Born_In_The_USA" title="Born In The USA">Born In The USA</a></i> as well as debuting a new song in honor of New Jersey and Giants Stadium entitled, "Wrecking Ball." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></li>
<li>October 24, 2009: The final soccer game at Giants Stadium was played between the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Red_Bulls" title="New York Red Bulls">New York Red Bulls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toronto_FC" title="Toronto FC">Toronto FC</a>, with New York winning 5–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></li>
<li>December 27, 2009: The Giants played their final home game in the stadium against the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Panthers" title="Carolina Panthers">Carolina Panthers</a>, losing by a score of 41–9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></li>
<li>January 3, 2010: The Jets defeated the <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bengals" title="Cincinnati Bengals">Cincinnati Bengals</a> 37–0 in the final game at Giants Stadium. The victory would also earn the Jets a playoff berth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Giants_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>Giants Stadium is featured in the 2008 film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Day_the_Earth_Stood_Still_(2008_film)" title="The Day the Earth Stood Still (2008 film)">The Day the Earth Stood Still</a></i>, where it is destroyed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nanites" title="Nanites">nanites</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2" style="background: #203731; color:white;">
<div>

<li>Founded in 1960</li>
<li>Formerly the <b>New York Titans</b> (1960–62)</li>
<li>Based in <b><a href="/wiki/East_Rutherford,_New_Jersey" title="East Rutherford, New Jersey"><span style="color:white">East Rutherford</span></a></b>, <b><a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey"><span style="color:white">New Jersey</span></a></b></li>
